# predit specs

These specs capture the locked design decisions for `predit`. Implementation must follow what's here. Anything not in a spec is open to design at implementation time, with the result then captured back here.

## Read order

### Foundations

1. [`00-overview.md`](00-overview.md) — what predit is and the three-layer mental model
2. [`01-repo-and-licensing.md`](01-repo-and-licensing.md) — repo visibility, license, public-flip plan
3. [`02-build-stack.md`](02-build-stack.md) — runtime, package manager, build, test, CLI library

### Surface area

4. [`03-cli.md`](03-cli.md) — command surface
5. [`04-shows-and-episodes.md`](04-shows-and-episodes.md) — `show.yaml`, `episode.yaml`, resolution order
6. [`05-pipelines.md`](05-pipelines.md) — pipeline manifest, harness runtime, stages
7. [`06-tool-registry.md`](06-tool-registry.md) — `Tool` interface, integration kinds, registry surface
8. [`07-audio-subsystem.md`](07-audio-subsystem.md) — Cuesheet, primitives, master clock
9. [`08-skills.md`](08-skills.md) — skill formats and scoping
10. [`09-export.md`](09-export.md) — NLE handoff (Premiere / CapCut / DaVinci / EDL)

### Installation and orchestration

11. [`10-installation-and-user-projects.md`](10-installation-and-user-projects.md) — harness vs user-project split, cache layout, resolution
12. [`11-agent-driven-production.md`](11-agent-driven-production.md) — philosophy and how the agent does production
13. [`12-checkpoint-protocol.md`](12-checkpoint-protocol.md) — checkpoint lifecycle, resume, sample sub-checkpoints
14. [`13-reviewer-protocol.md`](13-reviewer-protocol.md) — self-review with CHAI rules
15. [`14-decision-log.md`](14-decision-log.md) — cumulative audit trail of material choices
16. [`15-announce-and-escalate.md`](15-announce-and-escalate.md) — decision communication contract
17. [`16-onboarding-and-discovery.md`](16-onboarding-and-discovery.md) — first-contact UX
18. [`17-self-review-of-output.md`](17-self-review-of-output.md) — final review of rendered output

## How to update a spec

Specs are living documents. When a decision changes:

1. Edit the relevant spec(s) in a single commit.
2. Reference the commit in the PR description that follows.
3. If the change invalidates code that already exists, that code is wrong as of this commit — open an issue.

# 00 — Overview

## What predit is

A show-first AI pre-production harness for video. The agent reads instructions (pipeline manifests, stage director skills, vendor knowledge skills) and drives the production stage by stage. The output is a rendered rough cut plus an editor handoff (EDL, Premiere XML, or CapCut draft) so a human editor can finish in their NLE of choice.

## The three-layer mental model

| Layer | Owns | Lives in | Reused across |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Show** | A brand / channel / identity: brand assets, recurring cast, the set of pipelines this show uses, per-pipeline defaults, ingest rules, publish destination | `shows/<show>/` | Episodes within the show |
| **Pipeline** | A workflow: stages, tools per stage, approval gates, audio-sync policy | `pipelines/<pipeline>.yaml` + `skills/pipelines/<pipeline>/` | Many shows |
| **Playbook** | A look: palette, typography, motion, audio mood | `playbooks/<playbook>.yaml` | Many shows / pipelines |

A show may declare and run **multiple pipelines**. A YouTube channel that publishes news raps and evergreen songs, or a consulting brand that publishes product demos and spokesperson videos, is one show with two pipelines — not two shows. The show owns the durable identity (brand, characters, voice); the pipelines are the workflows that identity runs.

The harness loads a show, resolves the episode's pipeline (a key in `show.pipelines`), merges per-pipeline defaults and the playbook, then runs the episode. The agent reads the resolved context and director skills to do the creative work at each stage.

## Episode is the unit of work

- One episode = one rendered output.
- Episodes live as `shows/<show>/episodes/<episode>.yaml` — author-intent only.
- Runtime state (current stage, costs, last checkpoint) lives in `projects/<show>/<episode>/` (gitignored).
- Generated media (images, video clips, narration, music, render) also lives under `projects/<show>/<episode>/`.

## Audio is the master clock for music-led content

Music videos, trailers, news-songs — anything where music drives the experience — use audio as the master clock. The audio subsystem detects sections, beats, and climax points; the scene planner snaps scene boundaries to those musical events. The visual cadence never overrides the audio.

For narration-led content (diaries, documentaries, explainers), voiceover is the master clock, and visuals snap to VO sections.

## Pre-production, not full post

`predit`'s job ends at "a rough cut you'd be happy to ship as draft + an editor handoff." A human editor finishes in Premiere, CapCut, or DaVinci. This boundary keeps `predit`'s scope tight and gives the output a credible home in existing professional workflows.

## Harness vs user project

`predit` is installed as a CLI. Users run it inside their own folder — a *user project* that contains only their shows, characters, brand assets, and runtime workspace. The harness ships bundled pipelines, playbooks, skills, schemas, and starter shows; the user project owns the actual content. See [`10-installation-and-user-projects.md`](10-installation-and-user-projects.md) for the resolution rules.

## Layer map

The system has three instruction layers:

1. **Tool layer** (`src/tools/`) — what exists, availability, cost, integration kind.
2. **Pipeline / skill layer** (`pipelines/`, `skills/pipelines/`) — how `predit` wants those tools used in a given workflow.
3. **Vendor knowledge layer** (`skills/agents/`) — provider-specific prompt engineering, parameter tuning.

Reading order for the agent: discover tools → read the relevant pipeline + director skill → read the vendor skill before crafting prompts.

 succeeded in 0ms:
# 10 — Installation and User Projects

## Two-repo model

`predit` is installed as a CLI. The user runs the CLI inside their **own** folder, which is owned by them — not by `predit`. This separates the harness (versioned, public, Apache 2.0) from user content (their shows, their characters, their music, their license).

```
┌────────────────────────────────┐         ┌────────────────────────────────┐
│  predit  (this repo)           │         │  <user-project>  (their repo)  │
│  ─────────────────────         │         │  ─────────────────────────     │
│  Source: src/                  │  ───▶   │  shows/, episodes/             │
│  Bundled: pipelines/,          │ install │  brand/, characters/           │
│           playbooks/,          │         │  music_library/, projects/     │
│           skills/, schemas/,   │         │  CLAUDE.md, AGENTS.md          │
│           starters/            │         │  .predit/ (cache, gitignored)  │
│  Apache 2.0, public            │         │  user-owned, user's license    │
└────────────────────────────────┘         └────────────────────────────────┘
```

## Installation

Global install:

```bash
pnpm add -g predit
# or
npm install -g predit
```

Per-project install (no global pollution):

```bash
pnpx predit init
# or
npx predit init
```

## User project lifecycle

### `predit init`

Scaffolds a new user project in the current directory:

```bash
cd ~/my-shows
predit init                       # creates CLAUDE.md, AGENTS.md, .predit/, .gitignore
predit init --git                 # same, plus `git init`
predit init --starter music-video # scaffold a starter show alongside the project
```

Created files:

```
my-shows/
├── CLAUDE.md                # tiny pointer → AGENTS.md
├── AGENTS.md                # agent operating contract for this project
├── .gitignore               # excludes .predit/, projects/, music_library/
├── .predit/                 # local cache of bundled harness content (gitignored)
│   ├── version.json
│   ├── pipelines/
│   ├── playbooks/
│   ├── skills/
│   │   ├── pipelines/<pipeline>/<stage>-director.md
│   │   ├── meta/<name>.md
│   │   └── agents/<name>.md
│   ├── schemas/
│   └── starters/
├── shows/                   # user content (initially empty)
├── music_library/           # gitignored drop zone
└── projects/                # gitignored runtime workspace
```

### `predit update`

Refreshes `.predit/` from the currently installed harness version. Detects mismatch automatically on every command and warns when stale. The user runs `predit update` to sync.

### `predit new show <slug> [--from <starter>]`

Creates `shows/<slug>/`. With `--from <starter>`, copies a starter template from `.predit/starters/<starter>/` as the initial content. Starters carry an example `show.yaml`, a brand stub, sample characters, and an episode template.

Available starters listed by `predit ls starters`.

## What is bundled vs user-owned

| Content | Lives in | Editable by user? |
|---|---|---|
| Source code | harness package | No (open-source PRs welcome) |
| Pipelines | `harness/pipelines/` → cached in `.predit/pipelines/` | Yes — override by placing same-named file in `<project>/pipelines/` |
| Playbooks | `harness/playbooks/` → cached in `.predit/playbooks/` | Yes — override in `<project>/playbooks/` |
| Director skills | `harness/skills/pipelines/...` → cached | Yes — override in `<project>/skills/pipelines/...` or per-show in `<project>/shows/<show>/skills/` |
| Meta skills | `harness/skills/meta/` → cached | Generally not — meta skills are the harness contract |
| Vendor skills (Layer 3) | `harness/skills/agents/` → cached | Yes — override in `<project>/skills/agents/` |
| Starters | `harness/starters/` → cached | No (cloned via `predit new show --from`, then user-edited) |
| Shows, characters, brand, episodes | `<project>/shows/` | Yes — fully user-owned |
| Music files, render outputs | `<project>/music_library/`, `<project>/projects/` | Yes (gitignored) |

## Resolution order

When the harness needs any resource (pipeline, playbook, skill, schema):

1. Check user project local path (`<project>/pipelines/<name>.yaml`, etc.).
2. Fall back to the cache (`<project>/.predit/pipelines/<name>.yaml`).
3. Error if neither exists.

User overrides always win. The bundled cache is read-only from the harness's perspective — `predit update` is the only thing that writes to it.

## Why a local cache instead of reading from `node_modules`

- Agents (Claude Code, Codex) navigate via filesystem reads. `.predit/skills/...` is a stable, predictable path inside the project. `node_modules/predit/...` is brittle (depends on install method, pnpm hoisting, global vs local).
- The cache is gitignored, so a fresh clone of the user's project doesn't carry stale harness content; `predit update` repopulates from whatever harness version is installed.
- The cache version is tracked in `.predit/version.json` so the harness can warn on mismatch and refuse to operate on a project cached against an incompatible major version.

## User project is user-owned

The user picks the license, the source-control host, the backup strategy, and what to publish. The harness has no opinion on whether their `shows/` directory is a public GitHub repo or a personal Backblaze backup. `predit` produces video; it does not manage user content.

## Multi-user / team scenarios

A team can share a user project the same way they share any git repo. The cached `.predit/` is gitignored — each contributor's `.predit/` reflects their locally installed harness version. Recommend pinning the harness version in a `predit.lock` file (future feature) so all collaborators stay in sync.

 succeeded in 0ms:
# 11 — Agent-Driven Production

## Philosophy

`predit` is instruction-driven. The agent (Claude Code, Codex, or any harness reading the same skill markdown) **is** the production intelligence — it reads instructions, makes decisions, calls tools, checks its own work, revises, and presents to the human for approval. The code is the orchestration shell; the markdown skills are the brain.

This means the agent's behavior can be improved by editing prose — without rebuilds, without releases, without code review. Adding a new pipeline is a YAML manifest plus a handful of Markdown director skills, not a Python or TypeScript refactor.

## What the agent does

For each episode, the agent works through the pipeline's stages. At every stage:

1. **Reads the stage director skill** in full before doing any work in that stage.
2. **Reads Layer 3 vendor skills** before calling any generation tool (image, video, TTS, music). Vendor skills carry provider-specific prompt structure, parameter sweet spots, quality keywords.
3. **Announces decisions before paid actions.** Tool name, provider, model, reason, sample-or-batch. The human is never surprised by a charge.
4. **Calls tools through the registry**, never directly. The registry handles availability, fallback, cost tracking.
5. **Produces the canonical artifact** declared by the stage in the pipeline manifest.
6. **Self-reviews** the artifact against the stage's `review_focus` and `success_criteria` (see [`13-reviewer-protocol.md`](13-reviewer-protocol.md)).
7. **Revises if review finds critical issues** — up to two rounds, then passes with warnings.
8. **Checkpoints the artifact** with status `completed` or `awaiting_human` (see [`12-checkpoint-protocol.md`](12-checkpoint-protocol.md)).
9. **Records material choices in the decision log** with rationale and rejected alternatives (see [`14-decision-log.md`](14-decision-log.md)).
10. **Presents to the human for approval** when the stage's `human_approval` is `required` (or `optional` and interactive mode).

## Adaptation to show types

Pipelines + playbooks + show defaults compose to express any show type. The agent reads the resolved configuration and adapts:

- A **music video** pipeline tells the agent to build a cuesheet, snap scenes to downbeats, and align the climax shot to the chorus.
- A **WWII diary** pipeline tells the agent to use VO as master clock, pace scenes to 4-8 second sepia stills, and call into the cinematic asset library.
- A **product demo** pipeline tells the agent to drive Remotion scenes around captured screen recordings, with a talking-head avatar overlay.
- A **news-song** pipeline tells the agent to interleave PS2-era generated visuals with real source screenshots from a `sources.yaml` file.

None of these require new code. They require a manifest, director skills per stage, and (optionally) a playbook for the look.

## The agent checks its own work

This is the load-bearing pattern. Every stage runs a reviewer pass before checkpointing, and major productions run additional self-reviews on the rendered output. The agent uses concrete criteria (loaded from the manifest, the playbook, and meta skills) to evaluate its own output, finds issues, proposes fixes, and revises. The CHAI rules (see [`13-reviewer-protocol.md`](13-reviewer-protocol.md)) require findings to be **accurate, complete, and constructive** — a critical finding without a concrete proposed fix is downgraded.

This self-review loop is why instruction-driven agents produce coherent video at all: the agent is allowed to make mistakes, but it is required to notice them and fix them before showing the human.

## Character sheets, brand assets, and the asset stage

Recurring characters live in `shows/<show>/characters/<name>/` with:

- `character.yaml` — voice ID, visual description, persona, references
- `references/` — optional reference images for image generation

When the asset stage runs, the agent reads the cast declared on the episode (`episode.cast: [rag, agent, graph]`), resolves each to its character directory, and includes the character sheet's visual description in image generation prompts. Consistency across episodes comes from the persisted character sheet — the agent does not re-invent the character per episode.

Brand assets (`shows/<show>/brand/`) work the same way: palette, logo, typography are read once and threaded through every stage that needs them.

## The orchestration layer is thin

The harness runner is a small state machine. It loads context, plans stages, loops over them, and dispatches each one to the agent with the right inputs. It does not make creative decisions, choose providers, write prompts, or evaluate quality. Those are all the agent's responsibility, guided by the skills.

If you can express a creative decision in prose, it belongs in a skill. If it requires conditional logic over filesystem state, schemas, or tool registry data, it belongs in the harness.

## Why this works

- **Agents pick up context from prose.** Modern LLM agents read markdown skills extremely well. Telling them "the chorus scene snaps to the first downbeat after the section start" is more reliable than encoding that logic in TypeScript and exposing a `getChorusAnchor()` function.
- **Revisability is in writing.** A bad scene-director skill is fixable by editing the markdown. A bad orchestration step in TypeScript needs a rebuild and a release.
- **Skills compose with show overrides.** A show can shadow any director skill (see [`08-skills.md`](08-skills.md)) without forking the pipeline. New show types emerge from new manifests + new skills, not new code.
- **Self-review keeps quality consistent.** The agent is reliable at applying explicit criteria (review focus, success criteria, playbook rules). Letting it review its own work catches the same mistakes a human reviewer would catch — at agent speed.

.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-47-raw.md:355:- [info] ImageHostInputSchema and ImageHostOutputSchema are defined in src/tools/catbox-host.ts and imported by s3-host.ts and r2-host.ts. Functional but couples two siblings to a third; consider moving shared host schemas to src/registry/image-host.ts. (unfixed)
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-47-raw.md:356:- [info] catbox_host.isAvailable() reads quota via process.cwd() because Tool.isAvailable() has no ctx parameter. Works for CLI invocation but means the quota file location is tied to where the harness is started rather than the project root passed at execute time. (unfixed)
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-47-raw.md:357:- [info] green_screen_processor 'fast' mode uses libvpx-vp9 which typically requires a .webm container; tests only exercise 'high' mode (prores_ks in .mov). A user passing output.mp4 with fast quality may get an ffmpeg container/codec error. Not a regression since this is a new tool. (unfixed)
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-47-raw.md:358:- [info] catbox_host.execute() calls recordUpload() before fetch(). A failed upload still increments the local daily counter. Acceptable for a soft-limit warning system but worth noting if users observe drift between predicted and actual quota usage. (unfixed)

.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-46-raw.md:349:- [info] ImageHostInputSchema and ImageHostOutputSchema are defined in src/tools/catbox-host.ts and imported by s3-host.ts and r2-host.ts. Functional but couples two siblings to a third; consider moving shared host schemas to src/registry/image-host.ts. (unfixed)
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-46-raw.md:350:- [info] catbox_host.isAvailable() reads quota via process.cwd() because Tool.isAvailable() has no ctx parameter. Works for CLI invocation but means the quota file location is tied to where the harness is started rather than the project root passed at execute time. (unfixed)
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-46-raw.md:351:- [info] green_screen_processor 'fast' mode uses libvpx-vp9 which typically requires a .webm container; tests only exercise 'high' mode (prores_ks in .mov). A user passing output.mp4 with fast quality may get an ffmpeg container/codec error. Not a regression since this is a new tool. (unfixed)
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-46-raw.md:352:- [info] catbox_host.execute() calls recordUpload() before fetch(). A failed upload still increments the local daily counter. Acceptable for a soft-limit warning system but worth noting if users observe drift between predicted and actual quota usage. (unfixed)

.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-43-raw.md:539:## Patterns
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-43-raw.md:540:- Separate validation logic from encoder invocation so blockers can stop composition before side effects.
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-43-raw.md:541:- Use focused unit tests for runtime mismatch, missing assets, timeline gaps, and unavailable runtimes.
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-43-raw.md:543:## Anti-Patterns
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-43-raw.md:544:- Avoid silently swapping render runtimes when the requested runtime is unavailable.
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-43-raw.md:545:- Avoid invoking encoders before all asset, timeline, and delivery-promise checks pass.
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-43-raw.md:547:## Suggested Skill Updates
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/learnings/issue-43-raw.md:548:- None.

.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/batch-implement.log:713:7. **Revises if review finds critical issues** — up to two rounds, then passes with warnings.
.alpha-loop/sessions/session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools/logs/batch-implement.log:731:This is the load-bearing pattern. Every stage runs a reviewer pass before checkpointing, and major productions run additional self-reviews on the rendered output. The agent uses concrete criteria (loaded from the manifest, the playbook, and meta skills) to evaluate its own output, finds issues, proposes fixes, and revises. The CHAI rules (see [`13-reviewer-protocol.md`](13-reviewer-protocol.md)) require findings to be **accurate, complete, and constructive** — a critical finding without a concrete proposed fix is downgraded.

## What Worked
- `ffprobe` was implemented with structured JSON parsing, zod validation, and typed error capture.
- FFmpeg-dependent tests used generated smoke fixtures and passed along with the full test suite.
- Typecheck passed with zero test-fix retries.

## What Failed
- Nothing

## Patterns
- Use `it.skipIf` for tests that depend on local binaries such as `ffmpeg` and `ffprobe`.
- Generate small media fixtures with FFmpeg lavfi inputs instead of committing binary fixtures.
- Wrap binary failures with command and stderr fields for actionable diagnostics.

## Anti-Patterns
- Avoid mixing adjacent epic work into a narrowly scoped issue run unless the batch explicitly calls for it.
- Do not leave verification empty when live binary behavior is part of the acceptance criteria.

## Suggested Skill Updates
- Add a testing pattern for optional external binary smoke tests using generated fixtures and `skipIf`.
- Add a tool-wrapper pattern requiring structured stderr capture, command echoing, and typed parse validation.

## What Worked
- Pre-compose validation and runtime routing were implemented with structured blocker handling.
- Tests and typecheck passed on the first attempt: 19 test files, 129 tests.

## What Failed
- Nothing.

## Patterns
- Separate validation logic from encoder invocation so blockers can stop composition before side effects.
- Use focused unit tests for runtime mismatch, missing assets, timeline gaps, and unavailable runtimes.

## Anti-Patterns
- Avoid silently swapping render runtimes when the requested runtime is unavailable.
- Avoid invoking encoders before all asset, timeline, and delivery-promise checks pass.

- None.

## What Worked
- Ported the Remotion scene and overlay catalog, including fixtures and routing helpers for all required scene types.
- Added cross-reference documentation in `bundled/skills/core/remotion.md`.
- `pnpm test` passed 157/157 tests and `pnpm typecheck` completed cleanly.

## What Failed
- Nothing.

## Patterns
- Pair each scene type with a Zod prop schema, fixture data, and a catalog entry.
- Use focused snapshot-style coverage through `src/remotion/scenes.test.ts` to verify every supported scene and overlay renders.
- Keep external binary-dependent tests guarded with `skipIf` capability checks.

## Anti-Patterns
- Avoid leaving verification output empty for visual/rendering work when a run has explicit visual acceptance criteria.
- Avoid bundling adjacent epic work into the same review summary unless the run is intentionally covering multiple issues.

## Suggested Skill Updates
- None.

- Implemented caption burn, HyperFrames adapter/gates, and playbook-to-CSS bridge with focused schemas and tests.
- `pnpm test` passed 25 files / 157 tests, and `pnpm typecheck` completed cleanly.
- Review confirmed issues #44 and #45 satisfy acceptance criteria.

## What Failed
- Nothing.
- No separate live verification output was captured beyond tests/typecheck.

## Patterns
- Use Zod artifact schemas for cuesheets/playbooks to keep adapter inputs explicit.
- Record external adapter phases in `render_report.validation_steps[]` so reviewers can verify lint/validate gates.
- Keep playbook styling as the shared source for Remotion captions and HyperFrames CSS variables.

## Anti-Patterns
- Do not invoke HyperFrames render if lint or validate fails.
- Do not use `@hyperframes/cli`; the public npm package is `hyperframes`.
- Avoid splitting visual styling logic across adapters instead of using the playbook bridge.

## Suggested Skill Updates
- Add a reviewer checklist item requiring `lint: ok` and `validate: ok` in `render_report.validation_steps[]`.
- Keep `bundled/skills/core/remotion.md` updated with caption burn and HyperFrames bridge guidance.

## What Worked
- All C-5 acceptance tools were implemented and auto-discovered through the registry.
- `pnpm test` passed with 175 tests and 1 skipped test; `pnpm typecheck` passed.
- Fixture-backed tests covered composition specialty behavior and ffmpeg/ffprobe integration.

## What Failed
- Nothing blocking; no test fix retries were needed.
- Four INFO review findings remained unfixed, mostly around shared schema placement, cwd-based quota lookup, and one green-screen codec/container risk.

## Patterns
- Tool adapters with Zod input/output schemas and registry discovery worked well for adding specialty composition tools.
- Media integration tests used generated ffmpeg fixtures and skipped cleanly when required binaries were unavailable.
- Remotion scene documentation was added as a catalog skill alongside code-level fixtures.

## Anti-Patterns
- Avoid importing shared schemas from sibling tool modules; move common contracts to shared registry or artifact modules.
- Avoid `process.cwd()` for tool availability checks when execution later uses an explicit project root.
- Test all codec/container quality branches for ffmpeg tools, not only the highest-quality happy path.

## Suggested Skill Updates
- `.alpha-loop/templates/skills/testing-patterns/SKILL.md`: add guidance to cover each ffmpeg quality/codec/container branch.
- `.alpha-loop/templates/skills/implementation-planning/SKILL.md`: add a reminder to place shared tool schemas in neutral shared modules.
- `.alpha-loop/templates/skills/code-review/SKILL.md`: add a checklist item for cwd-sensitive tool availability behavior.

## What Worked
- Image generation routing, ergonomic wrapper, and image hosting backends were implemented with registry coverage.
- Catbox, S3, and R2 hosting paths had focused tests, including quota tracking behavior.
- `pnpm test` and `pnpm typecheck` passed with 175 tests passing and 0 retries.

## What Failed
- Nothing.
- Review reported only INFO-level follow-ups, with no blocking acceptance or test failures.

## Patterns
- Capability-based registry selection worked well for adding `image_generation` and `image_hosting` without special-case orchestration.
- Backend-specific host tools reused a common input/output contract and were validated through small targeted tests.
- Environment-configured provider backends kept S3 and R2 pluggable while preserving Catbox as the default.

## Anti-Patterns
- Shared image host schemas living in `catbox-host.ts` couple sibling providers to one backend.
- Quota tracking behavior is partly tied to `process.cwd()` and increments before upload success, which can create confusing drift.
- Run artifacts referenced both #46 and #47, making issue attribution less clean than it should be.

## Suggested Skill Updates
- Update `.agents/skills/code-review/SKILL.md` to flag shared schema definitions placed inside one provider implementation.
- Update `.agents/skills/implementation-planning/SKILL.md` to require explicit quota accounting semantics for provider tools.
- Update `.agents/skills/testing-patterns/SKILL.md` to encourage failure-path tests for quota/state mutations around external calls.

## What Worked
- Implemented the C-7 provider set and registered image generation tools with cost tracking.
- `pnpm test` passed: 34 files, 185 tests passed, 1 skipped.
- `pnpm typecheck` passed with zero test-fix retries.

## What Failed
- Nothing reported.
- Manual fixture-generation verification output was not captured.

## Patterns
- Keep provider tools behind the registry contract so availability, invocation, outputs, and costs are tested consistently.
- Use provider-specific env checks and tests instead of requiring live credentials in unit tests.
- Track cost per call as part of tool execution, not as a separate caller responsibility.

## Anti-Patterns
- Do not leave manual checklist items without recorded artifact paths or verification logs.
- Avoid broad unrelated file changes in provider-focused issues unless they are required by shared contracts.

## Suggested Skill Updates
- Add a note to image-generation/tool-authoring guidance requiring manual fixture output paths and cost-log evidence for API image providers.

# Session Summary: session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools

## Overview
- Epic 5 completed cleanly: 9 issues succeeded, all with zero test-fix retries, and the suite/typecheck stayed green throughout.
- The strongest execution pattern was consistent use of `defineTool`, registry discovery, Zod contracts, focused tests, and environment/binary-gated behavior for optional integrations.
- The main weakness was verification hygiene: several issues passed automated checks but did not record manual, live, visual, or fixture artifact evidence.

## Recurring Patterns
- Tool/provider additions worked best as separate `defineTool` modules with Zod input/output schemas and registry auto-discovery.
- Optional binaries, local models, API credentials, and provider backends were handled well with availability probes and `skipIf`-guarded tests.
- Generated media fixtures avoided committed binary assets while still giving ffmpeg, Remotion, Mermaid, Manim, and stock/image tools practical coverage.
- Structured validation before side effects was effective: pre-compose blockers, runtime availability checks, and `render_report.validation_steps[]` gave reviewers deterministic evidence.
- Capability-based selection scaled cleanly across `video_compose`, `image_generation`, and `image_hosting`.

## Recurring Anti-Patterns
- Verification output was often missing or skipped even when acceptance criteria called for manual fixture queries, live binary behavior, rendered visuals, or generated artifact paths.
- Some run artifacts mixed issue context or bundled adjacent issue details, making attribution less clean than it should be.
- Shared schemas sometimes lived inside one provider/tool module, coupling sibling implementations.
- A few stateful behaviors were under-specified: `process.cwd()`-based availability, quota tracking location, and whether quota increments happen before or after successful uploads.
- Some media-tool tests covered only the happy path, leaving codec/container branches and failure-path state mutations as residual risk.

## Recommendations
- Update the implement prompt to require an “acceptance evidence” block: each manual/live/visual criterion must list an artifact path, command output, or explicit blocked reason.
- Add an Alpha Loop post-check that warns or fails when `verifySkipped: true` appears on issues whose acceptance text includes “manual,” “fixture,” “render,” “visual,” “binary,” or “produces an image.”
- Update `.alpha-loop/templates/skills/testing-patterns/SKILL.md` with patterns for optional external binary tests, generated media fixtures, ffmpeg codec/container branch coverage, and failure-path state mutation tests.
- Update `.alpha-loop/templates/skills/implementation-planning/SKILL.md` to require neutral shared modules for common provider schemas and explicit quota/accounting semantics for stateful tools.
- Update `.alpha-loop/templates/skills/code-review/SKILL.md` to flag provider schemas stored in one backend, `process.cwd()`-sensitive availability checks, and side effects that occur before external-call success.
- Clean up repeated plugin/skill loader warnings in project config: default prompts over limit, too many prompts, and skill icon paths containing `..`.

## Metrics
| Metric | Value |
|--------|-------|
| Issues processed | 9 |
| Success rate | 100% |
| Avg duration | 764s |
| Total duration | 115 min |

# Session Summary: session/epic-120-epic-5-composition-visual-tools

## Overview
- Epic 5 completed cleanly: 9 issues succeeded, all with zero test-fix retries, and the suite/typecheck stayed green throughout.
- The strongest execution pattern was consistent use of `defineTool`, registry discovery, Zod contracts, focused tests, and environment/binary-gated behavior for optional integrations.
- The main weakness was verification hygiene: several issues passed automated checks but did not record manual, live, visual, or fixture artifact evidence.

## Recurring Patterns
- Tool/provider additions worked best as separate `defineTool` modules with Zod input/output schemas and registry auto-discovery.
- Optional binaries, local models, API credentials, and provider backends were handled well with availability probes and `skipIf`-guarded tests.
- Generated media fixtures avoided committed binary assets while still giving ffmpeg, Remotion, Mermaid, Manim, and stock/image tools practical coverage.
- Structured validation before side effects was effective: pre-compose blockers, runtime availability checks, and `render_report.validation_steps[]` gave reviewers deterministic evidence.
- Capability-based selection scaled cleanly across `video_compose`, `image_generation`, and `image_hosting`.

## Recurring Anti-Patterns
- Verification output was often missing or skipped even when acceptance criteria called for manual fixture queries, live binary behavior, rendered visuals, or generated artifact paths.
- Some run artifacts mixed issue context or bundled adjacent issue details, making attribution less clean than it should be.
- Shared schemas sometimes lived inside one provider/tool module, coupling sibling implementations.
- A few stateful behaviors were under-specified: `process.cwd()`-based availability, quota tracking location, and whether quota increments happen before or after successful uploads.
- Some media-tool tests covered only the happy path, leaving codec/container branches and failure-path state mutations as residual risk.

## Recommendations
- Update the implement prompt to require an “acceptance evidence” block: each manual/live/visual criterion must list an artifact path, command output, or explicit blocked reason.
- Add an Alpha Loop post-check that warns or fails when `verifySkipped: true` appears on issues whose acceptance text includes “manual,” “fixture,” “render,” “visual,” “binary,” or “produces an image.”
- Update `.alpha-loop/templates/skills/testing-patterns/SKILL.md` with patterns for optional external binary tests, generated media fixtures, ffmpeg codec/container branch coverage, and failure-path state mutation tests.
- Update `.alpha-loop/templates/skills/implementation-planning/SKILL.md` to require neutral shared modules for common provider schemas and explicit quota/accounting semantics for stateful tools.
- Update `.alpha-loop/templates/skills/code-review/SKILL.md` to flag provider schemas stored in one backend, `process.cwd()`-sensitive availability checks, and side effects that occur before external-call success.
- Clean up repeated plugin/skill loader warnings in project config: default prompts over limit, too many prompts, and skill icon paths containing `..`.
